31.08.2025, 22:36 - Wojtek: TL;DR chciaÅ‚em zrobiÄ‡ own cache z labÃ³w
31.08.2025, 22:36 - Wojtek: Hi!

I'd like to share an idea that recently popped into my head.

In Poland (and some neighboring countries), we have an alternative "open" version of the geocaching platform called Opencaching. There are some differences between Opencaching and Geocaching. One of them is the "own cache" type, which is not available on Geocaching. Own cache is often a field-puzzle geocache that travels with the owner from event to event and can be logged as "found" when you contact the owner, complete the required task, and sign the logbook. Due to its nature, it has dynamic coordinates that need to be updated by the owner, indicating where the own geocache can be solved at the moment. From the Opencaching wiki:

"Own cache is a type of geocache whose final container, containing the logbook, remains under the control of the founder or maintainer. Boxes of this type do not need to have a fixed location defined by coordinates. To obtain them, contact (personal, email, phone, etc.) with the founder or maintainer is required. The founder may require additional steps (solving a puzzle, math, manual, or other task) before making a logbook entry."

The idea is unique and, of course, has its drawbacks. However, it can be leveraged in an amazing way. Iâ€™ve heard about own geocaches that require you to solve a Rubik's cube during an event or throw something a certain distance to obtain the lock code. The imagination is the only limit. The two major advantages of such a geocache type are that you have to interact with the owner, and more importantly, the owner takes care of it, so it might be really fancy without a threat of being stolen or damaged by muggles.

I had never thought of how to migrate this idea to Geocaching until the last MEGA event in Slovakia. Among the MEGA event lab adventures published there, I saw on the map that there is a mysterious MountainNinja's UFO lab: https://labs.geocaching.com/goto/0b85b25d-88e1-486d-8b80-63d25e387b21

It turns out that this is a single-stage lab adventure that "goes" with the owner to any event he attends. It has a pretty large location range (the current maximum, I believe) and it contains only one simple multi-answer question: who is the owner of this lab?

I think you know where I'm going with this :-D One can create an "own cache" geocache on geocaching.com with an Adventure Lab credit. Just create any field puzzle you want and bring it with you to the events you attend. The puzzle solution can then be used to answer the lab step. To complete it, people must contact you, solve whatever you have prepared for them, and claim the find by answering the lab. The only thing you need to do is to update the AL coordinates before the events, like MountainNinja does. And you can have up to 5 "own geocaches" with a single lab credit!

What do you think about this idea? I'd love to hear some comments on this topic. Unfortunately, I couldn't create an experimental "lab own cache" for myself because I do not have any AL credit right now. However, I couldn't wait longer to share this idea with you :-D

All the best,
kranfagel (Wojtek)
